In the deallocate method (lines 260-275), at line 265, the buffer is cleared and added back to the free list: `this.free.add(buffer);`\n\nNow, let me understand the race condition by looking at how buffers are allocated and how the batch sends data. The key insight from the task description is:\n\"when an in-flight ProducerBatch expires or its broker disconnects, the batch's pooled ByteBuffer is returned to the BufferPool and immediately reused by a new batch — while the original batch's request is still being written to the network by the Sender thread.\"\n\nSo the flow is:\n1. I found the key issue! At line 582, `builder.build(version)` is called immediately in the doSend method! This builds the request, which includes the MemoryRecords and their underlying ByteBuffer.\n\nThen at line 608, `request.toSend(header)` is called, which serializes the request into a Send object (which wraps the ByteBuffer(s)).\n\nThen at line 617, `selector.send(new NetworkSend(...))` is called to actually send the data.\n\nThe race condition is:1. The request is built at line 582 (this builds the actual request with the buffer contents)2. The request is added to inFlightRequests at line 616 3. Meanwhile, in the same Sender.run() loop or the next iteration:\n   - At line 406-407, getExpiredInflightBatches() is called\n   - At line 418, failBatch() is called for any expired batches\n   - At line 835, maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch() is called\n   - At line 174 in RecordAccumulator.deallocate(), the buffer is returned to the BufferPool\n   - At line 265 in BufferPool.deallocate(), the buffer is cleared and added to the free list\n2. A new batch can allocate the same buffer from the free list (it's been cleared, so it looks \"free\")\n5. The new batch writes to the buffer, corrupting the data that the Send object is trying to write\n\nThe key issue is that the buffer is returned to the pool while it's still in-flight. The fix should be to NOT deallocate the buffer for in-flight batches until they've actually been sent by the network layer.\n\n\nWhen an in-flight batch expires and failBatch() is invoked, the buffer gets deallocated immediately even though the Send object still holds a reference to it in the NetworkClient's queue. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01HqHSNgBYaPcnAZFxWxkiUH","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_014J3i7u9MB7hDVavs3beiCA","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/logs/agent/solution.md","content":"# Kafka Producer Buffer Pool Reuse Race Condition Analysis\n\n## Files Examined\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java` — Entry point for producer batch sending and failure handling\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/RecordAccumulator.java` — Batch accumulation and buffer deallocation\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/BufferPool.java` — Memory buffer management and reuse\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/ProducerBatch.java` — Individual batch structure holding buffer references\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/NetworkClient.java` — Network request serialization and in-flight tracking\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n1. **Entry point**: `Sender.sendProducerData()` (line 357)\n   - Drains ready batches from accumulator at line 395\n   - Adds them to inFlightBatches at line 396\n   - Calls sendProduceRequests() at line 442 to queue network sends\n\n2. **Request serialization**: `NetworkClient.doSend()` (line 551)\n   - Builds the request at line 582: `builder.build(version)`\n   - Creates Send object at line 608: `request.toSend(header)`\n   - Adds Send to inFlightRequests at line 616\n   - Queues to selector at line 617: `selector.send(new NetworkSend(...))`\n\n3. **Batch expiration check**: `Sender.sendProducerData()` (line 406-407)\n   - Calls `getExpiredInflightBatches(now)` which iterates inFlightBatches\n   - Removes expired batches from inFlightBatches at line 191\n\n4. **Batch failure handling**: `Sender.failBatch()` (line 817)\n   - Calls `batch.completeExceptionally()` at line 825\n   - Calls `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` at line 835\n\n5. **Buffer deallocation**: `RecordAccumulator.deallocate()` (line 1027)\n   - Calls `free.deallocate(batch.buffer(), batch.initialCapacity())` at line 1032\n\n6. **Buffer reuse**: `BufferPool.deallocate()` (line 260)\n   - Clears buffer at line 264: `buffer.clear()`\n   - Adds to free list at line 265: `this.free.add(buffer)`\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**File**: `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java`\n**Function**: `failBatch()` (line 817) and `sendProducerData()` (line 357)\n**Line**: ~835 (in failBatch) and ~418 (calling failBatch)\n\n### Why the Bug Occurs\n\nThe race condition happens because:\n\n1. **Request sent asynchronously**: When `sendProduceRequest()` calls `client.send()` at line 914, the request is NOT immediately written to the socket. Instead, it's queued in the NetworkClient and will be serialized and sent by the network I/O thread when the socket is ready.\n\n2. **Request holds buffer reference**: The NetworkClient's `doSend()` method (line 608) calls `request.toSend(header)` which creates a `Send` object containing references to the batch's ByteBuffer. This Send object is held in `inFlightRequests` (line 616).\n\n3. **Expired batch deallocates buffer immediately**: When `Sender.sendProducerData()` checks for expired in-flight batches (line 406-407):\n   - `getExpiredInflightBatches()` removes the batch from `inFlightBatches` (line 191)\n   - `failBatch()` is called at line 418\n   - Inside `failBatch()`, `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` is called at line 835\n   - This calls `accumulator.deallocate()` which returns the buffer to the BufferPool (line 1032)\n   - The buffer is cleared and added to the free list (line 265)\n\n4. **Buffer reused while still in-flight**: The buffer is now available in the free list, even though the Send object in NetworkClient's `inFlightRequests` still holds a reference to it and may still be writing it to the socket.\n\n5. **Corruption occurs**: A new batch allocates the same buffer from the free list (via `accumulator.allocate()`), writes its data to it, and modifies its contents. Meanwhile, the original Send object is still writing to the socket, but the buffer now contains corrupted data from the new batch.\n\n### The Core Issue\n\nThe key vulnerability is at **line 835 in Sender.java**:\n```java\nmaybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);  // Called in failBatch()\n```\n\nThis line deallocates the buffer for a batch that is still in-flight in the NetworkClient. The batch's request may still be queued in the selector, waiting to be written to the socket, or currently being written. The Send object holds a reference to the ByteBuffer, not a copy of it.\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\nThe fix requires separating buffer deallocation from batch failure handling. When a batch expires while in-flight, we should NOT deallocate its buffer immediately. Instead, we should:\n\n1. Mark the batch as failed\n2. Let the buffer remain allocated and referenced by the in-flight Send object\n3. Deallocate the buffer only when the response is received (in `completeBatch()`) or when the network connection is definitively closed\n\n### Implementation\n\n**Modification to Sender.java, failBatch() method (line 817-836)**:\n\n```diff\nprivate void failBatch(\n    ProducerBatch batch,\n    RuntimeException topLevelException,\n    Function<Integer, RuntimeException> recordExceptions,\n    boolean adjustSequenceNumbers\n) {\n    this.sensors.recordErrors(batch.topicPartition.topic(), batch.recordCount);\n\n    if (batch.completeExceptionally(topLevelException, recordExceptions)) {\n        if (transactionManager != null) {\n            try {\n                transactionManager.handleFailedBatch(batch, topLevelException, adjustSequenceNumbers);\n            } catch (Exception e) {\n                log.debug(\"Encountered error when transaction manager was handling a failed batch\", e);\n            }\n        }\n-       maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n+       // For in-flight batches, don't deallocate the buffer here.\n+       // The buffer is still referenced by the Send object in the NetworkClient.\n+       // We'll deallocate it when the response is received (in completeBatch)\n+       // or when the network connection closes.\n+       maybeRemoveFromInflightBatches(batch);\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThis change ensures that:\n- The batch is still tracked until its request completes\n- The buffer stays allocated and under the control of the in-flight Send object\n- Deallocation happens safely in `completeBatch()` after the response is received\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Execution Path to Race Condition\n\n1. Producer calls `Sender.run()` which calls `runOnce()`\n2. `runOnce()` calls `sendProducerData()` at line 339\n3. Batches are drained and sent via `sendProduceRequest()` (lines 395, 442)\n4. In NetworkClient, request is built and Send object is created (line 608)\n5. Send object is queued to selector, awaiting network I/O (line 617)\n6. Meanwhile, in the next `sendProducerData()` call, batch expiration is checked (line 406)\n7. Expired batch is found and removed from inFlightBatches (line 191)\n8. `failBatch()` is called, which deallocates the buffer (line 835)\n9. Buffer is returned to pool and added to free list (line 265)\n10. New batch allocates same buffer, writes to it\n11. Original Send object writes corrupted data to socket\n12. Messages intended for topic A have topic B data, or vice versa\n\n### Why CRC Passes\n\nThe CRC checksum in Kafka only covers the record key/value/headers, not the topic/partition metadata. The partition information is in the ProduceRequest header (serialized separately). When the buffer is reused mid-write, the corruption affects the message payload, but since the CRC was already embedded when the batch was created, it doesn't detect the corruption if only the buffer contents were overwritten after CRC calculation.\n\n### Impact\n\nThis bug manifests as messages silently appearing on wrong topics, especially during:\n- Network disruptions or broker restarts (causing timeouts)\n- High latency scenarios with lingering enabled (`linger.ms > 0`)\n- Burst traffic that triggers batch expiration\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":8,"cache_creation_input_tokens":5018,"cache_read_input_tokens":85529,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":5018},"output_tokens":3,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"b832c745-1522-47db-9dd3-36e6715f0352","uuid":"f397351e-fffe-4957-978e-de3847e9c56d"}
{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_014J3i7u9MB7hDVavs3beiCA","type":"tool_result","content":"File created successfully at: /logs/agent/solution.md"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"b832c745-1522-47db-9dd3-36e6715f0352","uuid":"0d95fd9a-6e9e-40c8-80d7-df46f3b2be6d","tool_use_result":{"type":"create","filePath":"/logs/agent/solution.md","content":"# Kafka Producer Buffer Pool Reuse Race Condition Analysis\n\n## Files Examined\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java` — Entry point for producer batch sending and failure handling\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/RecordAccumulator.java` — Batch accumulation and buffer deallocation\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/BufferPool.java` — Memory buffer management and reuse\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/ProducerBatch.java` — Individual batch structure holding buffer references\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/NetworkClient.java` — Network request serialization and in-flight tracking\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n1. **Entry point**: `Sender.sendProducerData()` (line 357)\n   - Drains ready batches from accumulator at line 395\n   - Adds them to inFlightBatches at line 396\n   - Calls sendProduceRequests() at line 442 to queue network sends\n\n2. **Request serialization**: `NetworkClient.doSend()` (line 551)\n   - Builds the request at line 582: `builder.build(version)`\n   - Creates Send object at line 608: `request.toSend(header)`\n   - Adds Send to inFlightRequests at line 616\n   - Queues to selector at line 617: `selector.send(new NetworkSend(...))`\n\n3. **Batch expiration check**: `Sender.sendProducerData()` (line 406-407)\n   - Calls `getExpiredInflightBatches(now)` which iterates inFlightBatches\n   - Removes expired batches from inFlightBatches at line 191\n\n4. **Batch failure handling**: `Sender.failBatch()` (line 817)\n   - Calls `batch.completeExceptionally()` at line 825\n   - Calls `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` at line 835\n\n5. **Buffer deallocation**: `RecordAccumulator.deallocate()` (line 1027)\n   - Calls `free.deallocate(batch.buffer(), batch.initialCapacity())` at line 1032\n\n6. **Buffer reuse**: `BufferPool.deallocate()` (line 260)\n   - Clears buffer at line 264: `buffer.clear()`\n   - Adds to free list at line 265: `this.free.add(buffer)`\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**File**: `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java`\n**Function**: `failBatch()` (line 817) and `sendProducerData()` (line 357)\n**Line**: ~835 (in failBatch) and ~418 (calling failBatch)\n\n### Why the Bug Occurs\n\nThe race condition happens because:\n\n1. **Request sent asynchronously**: When `sendProduceRequest()` calls `client.send()` at line 914, the request is NOT immediately written to the socket. Instead, it's queued in the NetworkClient and will be serialized and sent by the network I/O thread when the socket is ready.\n\n2. **Request holds buffer reference**: The NetworkClient's `doSend()` method (line 608) calls `request.toSend(header)` which creates a `Send` object containing references to the batch's ByteBuffer. This Send object is held in `inFlightRequests` (line 616).\n\n3. **Expired batch deallocates buffer immediately**: When `Sender.sendProducerData()` checks for expired in-flight batches (line 406-407):\n   - `getExpiredInflightBatches()` removes the batch from `inFlightBatches` (line 191)\n   - `failBatch()` is called at line 418\n   - Inside `failBatch()`, `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` is called at line 835\n   - This calls `accumulator.deallocate()` which returns the buffer to the BufferPool (line 1032)\n   - The buffer is cleared and added to the free list (line 265)\n\n4. **Buffer reused while still in-flight**: The buffer is now available in the free list, even though the Send object in NetworkClient's `inFlightRequests` still holds a reference to it and may still be writing it to the socket.\n\n5. **Corruption occurs**: A new batch allocates the same buffer from the free list (via `accumulator.allocate()`), writes its data to it, and modifies its contents. Meanwhile, the original Send object is still writing to the socket, but the buffer now contains corrupted data from the new batch.\n\n### The Core Issue\n\nThe key vulnerability is at **line 835 in Sender.java**:\n```java\nmaybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);  // Called in failBatch()\n```\n\nThis line deallocates the buffer for a batch that is still in-flight in the NetworkClient. The batch's request may still be queued in the selector, waiting to be written to the socket, or currently being written. The Send object holds a reference to the ByteBuffer, not a copy of it.\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\nThe fix requires separating buffer deallocation from batch failure handling. When a batch expires while in-flight, we should NOT deallocate its buffer immediately. Instead, we should:\n\n1. Mark the batch as failed\n2. Let the buffer remain allocated and referenced by the in-flight Send object\n3. Deallocate the buffer only when the response is received (in `completeBatch()`) or when the network connection is definitively closed\n\n### Implementation\n\n**Modification to Sender.java, failBatch() method (line 817-836)**:\n\n```diff\nprivate void failBatch(\n    ProducerBatch batch,\n    RuntimeException topLevelException,\n    Function<Integer, RuntimeException> recordExceptions,\n    boolean adjustSequenceNumbers\n) {\n    this.sensors.recordErrors(batch.topicPartition.topic(), batch.recordCount);\n\n    if (batch.completeExceptionally(topLevelException, recordExceptions)) {\n        if (transactionManager != null) {\n            try {\n                transactionManager.handleFailedBatch(batch, topLevelException, adjustSequenceNumbers);\n            } catch (Exception e) {\n                log.debug(\"Encountered error when transaction manager was handling a failed batch\", e);\n            }\n        }\n-       maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n+       // For in-flight batches, don't deallocate the buffer here.\n+       // The buffer is still referenced by the Send object in the NetworkClient.\n+       // We'll deallocate it when the response is received (in completeBatch)\n+       // or when the network connection closes.\n+       maybeRemoveFromInflightBatches(batch);\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThis change ensures that:\n- The batch is still tracked until its request completes\n- The buffer stays allocated and under the control of the in-flight Send object\n- Deallocation happens safely in `completeBatch()` after the response is received\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Execution Path to Race Condition\n\n1. Producer calls `Sender.run()` which calls `runOnce()`\n2. `runOnce()` calls `sendProducerData()` at line 339\n3. Batches are drained and sent via `sendProduceRequest()` (lines 395, 442)\n4. In NetworkClient, request is built and Send object is created (line 608)\n5. Send object is queued to selector, awaiting network I/O (line 617)\n6. Meanwhile, in the next `sendProducerData()` call, batch expiration is checked (line 406)\n7. Expired batch is found and removed from inFlightBatches (line 191)\n8. `failBatch()` is called, which deallocates the buffer (line 835)\n9. Buffer is returned to pool and added to free list (line 265)\n10. New batch allocates same buffer, writes to it\n11. Original Send object writes corrupted data to socket\n12. Messages intended for topic A have topic B data, or vice versa\n\n### Why CRC Passes\n\nThe CRC checksum in Kafka only covers the record key/value/headers, not the topic/partition metadata. The partition information is in the ProduceRequest header (serialized separately). When the buffer is reused mid-write, the corruption affects the message payload, but since the CRC was already embedded when the batch was created, it doesn't detect the corruption if only the buffer contents were overwritten after CRC calculation.\n\n### Impact\n\nThis bug manifests as messages silently appearing on wrong topics, especially during:\n- Network disruptions or broker restarts (causing timeouts)\n- High latency scenarios with lingering enabled (`linger.ms > 0`)\n- Burst traffic that triggers batch expiration\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

The expiration just marks it as failed, but the network layer must finish using it first.","originalFile":"# Kafka Producer Buffer Pool Reuse Race Condition Analysis\n\n## Files Examined\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java` — Entry point for producer batch sending and failure handling\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/RecordAccumulator.java` — Batch accumulation and buffer deallocation\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/BufferPool.java` — Memory buffer management and reuse\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/ProducerBatch.java` — Individual batch structure holding buffer references\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/NetworkClient.java` — Network request serialization and in-flight tracking\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n1. **Entry point**: `Sender.sendProducerData()` (line 357)\n   - Drains ready batches from accumulator at line 395\n   - Adds them to inFlightBatches at line 396\n   - Calls sendProduceRequests() at line 442 to queue network sends\n\n2. **Request serialization**: `NetworkClient.doSend()` (line 551)\n   - Builds the request at line 582: `builder.build(version)`\n   - Creates Send object at line 608: `request.toSend(header)`\n   - Adds Send to inFlightRequests at line 616\n   - Queues to selector at line 617: `selector.send(new NetworkSend(...))`\n\n3. **Batch expiration check**: `Sender.sendProducerData()` (line 406-407)\n   - Calls `getExpiredInflightBatches(now)` which iterates inFlightBatches\n   - Removes expired batches from inFlightBatches at line 191\n\n4. **Batch failure handling**: `Sender.failBatch()` (line 817)\n   - Calls `batch.completeExceptionally()` at line 825\n   - Calls `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` at line 835\n\n5. **Buffer deallocation**: `RecordAccumulator.deallocate()` (line 1027)\n   - Calls `free.deallocate(batch.buffer(), batch.initialCapacity())` at line 1032\n\n6. **Buffer reuse**: `BufferPool.deallocate()` (line 260)\n   - Clears buffer at line 264: `buffer.clear()`\n   - Adds to free list at line 265: `this.free.add(buffer)`\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**File**: `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java`\n**Function**: `failBatch()` (line 817) and `sendProducerData()` (line 357)\n**Line**: ~835 (in failBatch) and ~418 (calling failBatch)\n\n### Why the Bug Occurs\n\nThe race condition happens because:\n\n1. **Request sent asynchronously**: When `sendProduceRequest()` calls `client.send()` at line 914, the request is NOT immediately written to the socket. Instead, it's queued in the NetworkClient and will be serialized and sent by the network I/O thread when the socket is ready.\n\n2. **Request holds buffer reference**: The NetworkClient's `doSend()` method (line 608) calls `request.toSend(header)` which creates a `Send` object containing references to the batch's ByteBuffer. This Send object is held in `inFlightRequests` (line 616).\n\n3. **Expired batch deallocates buffer immediately**: When `Sender.sendProducerData()` checks for expired in-flight batches (line 406-407):\n   - `getExpiredInflightBatches()` removes the batch from `inFlightBatches` (line 191)\n   - `failBatch()` is called at line 418\n   - Inside `failBatch()`, `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` is called at line 835\n   - This calls `accumulator.deallocate()` which returns the buffer to the BufferPool (line 1032)\n   - The buffer is cleared and added to the free list (line 265)\n\n4. **Buffer reused while still in-flight**: The buffer is now available in the free list, even though the Send object in NetworkClient's `inFlightRequests` still holds a reference to it and may still be writing it to the socket.\n\n5. **Corruption occurs**: A new batch allocates the same buffer from the free list (via `accumulator.allocate()`), writes its data to it, and modifies its contents. Meanwhile, the original Send object is still writing to the socket, but the buffer now contains corrupted data from the new batch.\n\n### The Core Issue\n\nThe key vulnerability is at **line 835 in Sender.java**:\n```java\nmaybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);  // Called in failBatch()\n```\n\nThis line deallocates the buffer for a batch that is still in-flight in the NetworkClient. The batch's request may still be queued in the selector, waiting to be written to the socket, or currently being written. The Send object holds a reference to the ByteBuffer, not a copy of it.\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\nThe fix requires separating buffer deallocation from batch failure handling. When a batch expires while in-flight, we should NOT deallocate its buffer immediately. Instead, we should:\n\n1. Mark the batch as failed\n2. Let the buffer remain allocated and referenced by the in-flight Send object\n3. Deallocate the buffer only when the response is received (in `completeBatch()`) or when the network connection is definitively closed\n\n### Implementation\n\n**Modification to Sender.java, failBatch() method (line 817-836)**:\n\n```diff\nprivate void failBatch(\n    ProducerBatch batch,\n    RuntimeException topLevelException,\n    Function<Integer, RuntimeException> recordExceptions,\n    boolean adjustSequenceNumbers\n) {\n    this.sensors.recordErrors(batch.topicPartition.topic(), batch.recordCount);\n\n    if (batch.completeExceptionally(topLevelException, recordExceptions)) {\n        if (transactionManager != null) {\n            try {\n                transactionManager.handleFailedBatch(batch, topLevelException, adjustSequenceNumbers);\n            } catch (Exception e) {\n                log.debug(\"Encountered error when transaction manager was handling a failed batch\", e);\n            }\n        }\n-       maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n+       // For in-flight batches, don't deallocate the buffer here.\n+       // The buffer is still referenced by the Send object in the NetworkClient.\n+       // We'll deallocate it when the response is received (in completeBatch)\n+       // or when the network connection closes.\n+       maybeRemoveFromInflightBatches(batch);\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThis change ensures that:\n- The batch is still tracked until its request completes\n- The buffer stays allocated and under the control of the in-flight Send object\n- Deallocation happens safely in `completeBatch()` after the response is received\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Execution Path to Race Condition\n\n1. Producer calls `Sender.run()` which calls `runOnce()`\n2. `runOnce()` calls `sendProducerData()` at line 339\n3. Batches are drained and sent via `sendProduceRequest()` (lines 395, 442)\n4. In NetworkClient, request is built and Send object is created (line 608)\n5. Send object is queued to selector, awaiting network I/O (line 617)\n6. Meanwhile, in the next `sendProducerData()` call, batch expiration is checked (line 406)\n7. Expired batch is found and removed from inFlightBatches (line 191)\n8. `failBatch()` is called, which deallocates the buffer (line 835)\n9. Buffer is returned to pool and added to free list (line 265)\n10. New batch allocates same buffer, writes to it\n11. Original Send object writes corrupted data to socket\n12. Messages intended for topic A have topic B data, or vice versa\n\n### Why CRC Passes\n\nThe CRC checksum in Kafka only covers the record key/value/headers, not the topic/partition metadata. The partition information is in the ProduceRequest header (serialized separately). When the buffer is reused mid-write, the corruption affects the message payload, but since the CRC was already embedded when the batch was created, it doesn't detect the corruption if only the buffer contents were overwritten after CRC calculation.\n\n### Impact\n\nThis bug manifests as messages silently appearing on wrong topics, especially during:\n- Network disruptions or broker restarts (causing timeouts)\n- High latency scenarios with lingering enabled (`linger.ms > 0`)\n- Burst traffic that triggers batch expiration\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":79,"oldLines":40,"newStart":79,"newLines":39,"lines":[" "," ### Implementation"," ","-**Modification to Sender.java, failBatch() method (line 817-836)**:","+The core issue is at **line 835 in Sender.java**, within the `failBatch()` method:"," ","+```java","+maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);  // UNSAFE for in-flight batches","+```","+","+This unconditionally deallocates the buffer, but the batch's request might still be queued in the NetworkClient's `inFlightRequests` (line 616 in NetworkClient.doSend()).","+","+**Solution: Don't deallocate buffers in failBatch() - let completeBatch() handle it**","+","+The fix requires modifying `failBatch()` to avoid deallocating buffers for batches that are still in-flight. The expiration just marks it as failed, but the network layer must finish using it first.\n\n### Why This Fix is Safe\n\nThe fix is safe because:\n\n1. **No double deallocation**: When a response arrives in `completeBatch()`, it calls `batch.complete()` which checks the batch's final state (line 218). If the batch was already marked as failed by `failBatch()`, then `complete()` returns false and `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` is NOT called (line 750).\n\n2. **Prevents corruption**: By not deallocating in `failBatch()`, the buffer remains valid while the `Send` object (still in NetworkClient's `inFlightRequests`) is writing to the socket.\n\n3. **Eventual cleanup**: When the response finally arrives or the connection closes:\n   - If response arrives: `completeBatch()` handles deallocation (though skipped due to final state check)\n   - If connection closes: The NetworkClient will clean up in-flight requests\n\n4. **Matches design intent**: Buffer pools are meant to manage buffer lifecycle. The expiration just marks it as failed, but the network layer must finish using it first.","newString":"**Key insight**: The buffer deallocation should happen at the END of the batch lifecycle (when response is received), not when the batch expires. The expiration just marks it as failed, but the network layer must finish using it first.\n\n### Why This Fix is Safe\n\nThe fix is safe because:\n\n1. **No double deallocation**: When a response arrives in `completeBatch()`, it calls `batch.complete()` which checks the batch's final state (line 218). If the batch was already marked as failed by `failBatch()`, then `complete()` returns false and `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` is NOT called (line 750).\n\n2. **Prevents corruption**: By not deallocating in `failBatch()`, the buffer remains valid while the `Send` object (still in NetworkClient's `inFlightRequests`) is writing to the socket.\n\n3. **Eventual cleanup**: When the response finally arrives or the connection closes:\n   - If response arrives: `completeBatch()` handles deallocation (though skipped due to final state check)\n   - If connection closes: The NetworkClient will clean up in-flight requests\n\n4. **Matches design intent**: Buffer pools are meant to manage buffer lifecycle. The accumulator should only deallocate when the batch lifecycle is truly complete (response received or connection error), not at expiration time.","originalFile":"# Kafka Producer Buffer Pool Reuse Race Condition Analysis\n\n## Files Examined\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java` — Entry point for producer batch sending and failure handling\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/RecordAccumulator.java` — Batch accumulation and buffer deallocation\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/BufferPool.java` — Memory buffer management and reuse\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/ProducerBatch.java` — Individual batch structure holding buffer references\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/NetworkClient.java` — Network request serialization and in-flight tracking\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n1. **Entry point**: `Sender.sendProducerData()` (line 357)\n   - Drains ready batches from accumulator at line 395\n   - Adds them to inFlightBatches at line 396\n   - Calls sendProduceRequests() at line 442 to queue network sends\n\n2. **Request serialization**: `NetworkClient.doSend()` (line 551)\n   - Builds the request at line 582: `builder.build(version)`\n   - Creates Send object at line 608: `request.toSend(header)`\n   - Adds Send to inFlightRequests at line 616\n   - Queues to selector at line 617: `selector.send(new NetworkSend(...))`\n\n3. **Batch expiration check**: `Sender.sendProducerData()` (line 406-407)\n   - Calls `getExpiredInflightBatches(now)` which iterates inFlightBatches\n   - Removes expired batches from inFlightBatches at line 191\n\n4. **Batch failure handling**: `Sender.failBatch()` (line 817)\n   - Calls `batch.completeExceptionally()` at line 825\n   - Calls `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` at line 835\n\n5. **Buffer deallocation**: `RecordAccumulator.deallocate()` (line 1027)\n   - Calls `free.deallocate(batch.buffer(), batch.initialCapacity())` at line 1032\n\n6. **Buffer reuse**: `BufferPool.deallocate()` (line 260)\n   - Clears buffer at line 264: `buffer.clear()`\n   - Adds to free list at line 265: `this.free.add(buffer)`\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**File**: `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java`\n**Function**: `failBatch()` (line 817) and `sendProducerData()` (line 357)\n**Line**: ~835 (in failBatch) and ~418 (calling failBatch)\n\n### Why the Bug Occurs\n\nThe race condition happens because:\n\n1. **Request sent asynchronously**: When `sendProduceRequest()` calls `client.send()` at line 914, the request is NOT immediately written to the socket. Instead, it's queued in the NetworkClient and will be serialized and sent by the network I/O thread when the socket is ready.\n\n2. **Request holds buffer reference**: The NetworkClient's `doSend()` method (line 608) calls `request.toSend(header)` which creates a `Send` object containing references to the batch's ByteBuffer. This Send object is held in `inFlightRequests` (line 616).\n\n3. **Expired batch deallocates buffer immediately**: When `Sender.sendProducerData()` checks for expired in-flight batches (line 406-407):\n   - `getExpiredInflightBatches()` removes the batch from `inFlightBatches` (line 191)\n   - `failBatch()` is called at line 418\n   - Inside `failBatch()`, `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` is called at line 835\n   - This calls `accumulator.deallocate()` which returns the buffer to the BufferPool (line 1032)\n   - The buffer is cleared and added to the free list (line 265)\n\n4. **Buffer reused while still in-flight**: The buffer is now available in the free list, even though the Send object in NetworkClient's `inFlightRequests` still holds a reference to it and may still be writing it to the socket.\n\n5. **Corruption occurs**: A new batch allocates the same buffer from the free list (via `accumulator.allocate()`), writes its data to it, and modifies its contents. Meanwhile, the original Send object is still writing to the socket, but the buffer now contains corrupted data from the new batch.\n\n### The Core Issue\n\nThe key vulnerability is at **line 835 in Sender.java**:\n```java\nmaybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);  // Called in failBatch()\n```\n\nThis line deallocates the buffer for a batch that is still in-flight in the NetworkClient. The batch's request may still be queued in the selector, waiting to be written to the socket, or currently being written. The Send object holds a reference to the ByteBuffer, not a copy of it.\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\nThe fix requires separating buffer deallocation from batch failure handling. When a batch expires while in-flight, we should NOT deallocate its buffer immediately. Instead, we should:\n\n1. Mark the batch as failed\n2. Let the buffer remain allocated and referenced by the in-flight Send object\n3. Deallocate the buffer only when the response is received (in `completeBatch()`) or when the network connection is definitively closed\n\n### Implementation\n\nThe core issue is at **line 835 in Sender.java**, within the `failBatch()` method:\n\n```java\nmaybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);  // UNSAFE for in-flight batches\n```\n\nThis unconditionally deallocates the buffer, but the batch's request might still be queued in the NetworkClient's `inFlightRequests` (line 616 in NetworkClient.doSend()).\n\n**Solution: Don't deallocate buffers in failBatch() - let completeBatch() handle it**\n\nThe fix requires modifying `failBatch()` to avoid deallocating buffers for batches that are still in-flight. Instead of:\n\n```diff\n- maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n```\n\nWe should:\n\n```diff\n+ // Don't deallocate buffer here - it's still in-flight in NetworkClient.\n+ // The buffer will be deallocated in completeBatch() when response arrives.\n+ // If response never arrives, the connection closure will clean it up.\n+ maybeRemoveFromInflightBatches(batch);\n```\n\nThis change ensures that:\n1. **The batch is removed from tracking** via `maybeRemoveFromInflightBatches()` (line 173)\n2. **The buffer remains allocated** while in-flight\n3. **Safe deallocation happens in completeBatch()** (line 750) when the response is received\n4. **No corruption occurs** because the Send object always has valid buffer contents\n\n**Key insight**: The buffer deallocation should happen at the END of the batch lifecycle (when response is received), not when the batch expires. The expiration just marks it as failed, but the network layer must finish using it first.\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Execution Path to Race Condition\n\n1. Producer calls `Sender.run()` which calls `runOnce()`\n2. `runOnce()` calls `sendProducerData()` at line 339\n3. Batches are drained and sent via `sendProduceRequest()` (lines 395, 442)\n4. In NetworkClient, request is built and Send object is created (line 608)\n5. Send object is queued to selector, awaiting network I/O (line 617)\n6. Meanwhile, in the next `sendProducerData()` call, batch expiration is checked (line 406)\n7. Expired batch is found and removed from inFlightBatches (line 191)\n8. `failBatch()` is called, which deallocates the buffer (line 835)\n9. Buffer is returned to pool and added to free list (line 265)\n10. New batch allocates same buffer, writes to it\n11. Original Send object writes corrupted data to socket\n12. Messages intended for topic A have topic B data, or vice versa\n\n### Why CRC Passes\n\nThe CRC checksum in Kafka only covers the record key/value/headers, not the topic/partition metadata. The partition information is in the ProduceRequest header (serialized separately). When the buffer is reused mid-write, the corruption affects the message payload, but since the CRC was already embedded when the batch was created, it doesn't detect the corruption if only the buffer contents were overwritten after CRC calculation.\n\n### Impact\n\nThis bug manifests as messages silently appearing on wrong topics, especially during:\n- Network disruptions or broker restarts (causing timeouts)\n- High latency scenarios with lingering enabled (`linger.ms > 0`)\n- Burst traffic that triggers batch expiration\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":112,"oldLines":6,"newStart":112,"newLines":20,"lines":[" "," **Key insight**: The buffer deallocation should happen at the END of the batch lifecycle (when response is received), not when the batch expires. The expiration just marks it as failed, but the network layer must finish using it first."," ","+### Why This Fix is Safe","+","+The fix is safe because:","+","+1. **No double deallocation**: When a response arrives in `completeBatch()`, it calls `batch.complete()` which checks the batch's final state (line 218). {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01EadBgBzwgtSJcgwMFrep7X","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Looking at this, I see the issue more clearly. The completeBatch() method at line 749 only calls maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch() if batch.complete() returns true. But if the batch was already completed (failed) by failBatch(), then batch.complete() returns false and nothing happens.\n\nSo my proposed fix needs to ensure that the buffer is deallocated even if the batch was already failed.Here's a better fix:1. In failBatch(), don't deallocate the buffer (to avoid the race condition)\n2. In completeBatch(), ALWAYS deallocate if the batch is already done (even if failed)\n\nActually, looking at the code again, I realize that the batch only has one final state at a time. If failBatch() sets it to FAILED, then when the response arrives, batch.complete() will check if the final state is already set. If it is, it returns false.So we need to handle the deallocation for already-failed batches in completeBatch().Here's the fix:```java\nprivate void completeBatch(ProducerBatch batch, ProduceResponse.PartitionResponse response) {\n    if (transactionManager != null) {\n        transactionManager.handleCompletedBatch(batch, response);\n    }\n\n    if (batch.complete(response.baseOffset, response.logAppendTime)) {\n        maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n    } else if (batch.isDone()) {\n        // Batch was already completed (likely failed due to expiration before response arrived)\n        // Still need to deallocate the buffer\n        maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n    }\n}\n```\n\nBut wait, this would cause double-deallocation if failBatch() also deallocates!With my original fix where failBatch() doesn't deallocate, this would ensure that:1. When batch fails due to expiration, failBatch() marks it as failed but doesn't deallocate\n\n\n2. When response arrives, completeBatch() deallocates (because batch.isDone() is true)\n3. No race condition because buffer is not deallocated until response arrives\n\nThis is the correct fix!Let me update the solution document with the precise fix after request is done** (when response arrives or connection closes)\n4. **No corruption occurs** because the batch's buffer is never reused while in-flight","originalFile":"# Kafka Producer Buffer Pool Reuse Race Condition Analysis\n\n## Files Examined\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java` — Entry point for producer batch sending and failure handling\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/RecordAccumulator.java` — Batch accumulation and buffer deallocation\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/BufferPool.java` — Memory buffer management and reuse\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/ProducerBatch.java` — Individual batch structure holding buffer references\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/NetworkClient.java` — Network request serialization and in-flight tracking\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n1. **Entry point**: `Sender.sendProducerData()` (line 357)\n   - Drains ready batches from accumulator at line 395\n   - Adds them to inFlightBatches at line 396\n   - Calls sendProduceRequests() at line 442 to queue network sends\n\n2. **Request serialization**: `NetworkClient.doSend()` (line 551)\n   - Builds the request at line 582: `builder.build(version)`\n   - Creates Send object at line 608: `request.toSend(header)`\n   - Adds Send to inFlightRequests at line 616\n   - Queues to selector at line 617: `selector.send(new NetworkSend(...))`\n\n3. **Batch expiration check**: `Sender.sendProducerData()` (line 406-407)\n   - Calls `getExpiredInflightBatches(now)` which iterates inFlightBatches\n   - Removes expired batches from inFlightBatches at line 191\n\n4. **Batch failure handling**: `Sender.failBatch()` (line 817)\n   - Calls `batch.completeExceptionally()` at line 825\n   - Calls `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` at line 835\n\n5. **Buffer deallocation**: `RecordAccumulator.deallocate()` (line 1027)\n   - Calls `free.deallocate(batch.buffer(), batch.initialCapacity())` at line 1032\n\n6. **Buffer reuse**: `BufferPool.deallocate()` (line 260)\n   - Clears buffer at line 264: `buffer.clear()`\n   - Adds to free list at line 265: `this.free.add(buffer)`\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**File**: `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java`\n**Function**: `failBatch()` (line 817) and `sendProducerData()` (line 357)\n**Line**: ~835 (in failBatch) and ~418 (calling failBatch)\n\n### Why the Bug Occurs\n\nThe race condition happens because:\n\n1. **Request sent asynchronously**: When `sendProduceRequest()` calls `client.send()` at line 914, the request is NOT immediately written to the socket. Instead, it's queued in the NetworkClient and will be serialized and sent by the network I/O thread when the socket is ready.\n\n2. **Request holds buffer reference**: The NetworkClient's `doSend()` method (line 608) calls `request.toSend(header)` which creates a `Send` object containing references to the batch's ByteBuffer. This Send object is held in `inFlightRequests` (line 616).\n\n3. **Expired batch deallocates buffer immediately**: When `Sender.sendProducerData()` checks for expired in-flight batches (line 406-407):\n   - `getExpiredInflightBatches()` removes the batch from `inFlightBatches` (line 191)\n   - `failBatch()` is called at line 418\n   - Inside `failBatch()`, `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` is called at line 835\n   - This calls `accumulator.deallocate()` which returns the buffer to the BufferPool (line 1032)\n   - The buffer is cleared and added to the free list (line 265)\n\n4. **Buffer reused while still in-flight**: The buffer is now available in the free list, even though the Send object in NetworkClient's `inFlightRequests` still holds a reference to it and may still be writing it to the socket.\n\n5. **Corruption occurs**: A new batch allocates the same buffer from the free list (via `accumulator.allocate()`), writes its data to it, and modifies its contents. Meanwhile, the original Send object is still writing to the socket, but the buffer now contains corrupted data from the new batch.\n\n### The Core Issue\n\nThe key vulnerability is at **line 835 in Sender.java**:\n```java\nmaybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);  // Called in failBatch()\n```\n\nThis line deallocates the buffer for a batch that is still in-flight in the NetworkClient. The batch's request may still be queued in the selector, waiting to be written to the socket, or currently being written. The Send object holds a reference to the ByteBuffer, not a copy of it.\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\nThe fix requires separating buffer deallocation from batch failure handling. When a batch expires while in-flight, we should NOT deallocate its buffer immediately. Instead, we should:\n\n1. Mark the batch as failed\n2. Let the buffer remain allocated and referenced by the in-flight Send object\n3. Deallocate the buffer only when the response is received (in `completeBatch()`) or when the network connection is definitively closed\n\n### Implementation\n\nThe core issue is at **line 835 in Sender.java**, within the `failBatch()` method:\n\n```java\nmaybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);  // UNSAFE for in-flight batches\n```\n\nThis unconditionally deallocates the buffer, but the batch's request might still be queued in the NetworkClient's `inFlightRequests` (line 616 in NetworkClient.doSend()).\n\n**Solution: Don't deallocate buffers in failBatch() - let completeBatch() handle it**\n\nThe fix requires modifying `failBatch()` to avoid deallocating buffers for batches that are still in-flight. Instead of:\n\n```diff\n- maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n```\n\nWe should:\n\n```diff\n+ // Don't deallocate buffer here - it's still in-flight in NetworkClient.\n+ // The buffer will be deallocated in completeBatch() when response arrives.\n+ // If response never arrives, the connection closure will clean it up.\n+ maybeRemoveFromInflightBatches(batch);\n```\n\nThis change ensures that:\n1. **The batch is removed from tracking** via `maybeRemoveFromInflightBatches()` (line 173)\n2. **The buffer remains allocated** while in-flight\n3. **Safe deallocation happens in completeBatch()** (line 750) when the response is received\n4. **No corruption occurs** because the Send object always has valid buffer contents\n\n**Key insight**: The buffer deallocation should happen at the END of the batch lifecycle (when response is received), not when the batch expires. The expiration just marks it as failed, but the network layer must finish using it first.\n\n### Why This Fix is Safe\n\nThe fix is safe because:\n\n1. **No double deallocation**: When a response arrives in `completeBatch()`, it calls `batch.complete()` which checks the batch's final state (line 218). If the batch was already marked as failed by `failBatch()`, then `complete()` returns false and `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` is NOT called (line 750).\n\n2. **Prevents corruption**: By not deallocating in `failBatch()`, the buffer remains valid while the `Send` object (still in NetworkClient's `inFlightRequests`) is writing to the socket.\n\n3. **Eventual cleanup**: When the response finally arrives or the connection closes:\n   - If response arrives: `completeBatch()` handles deallocation (though skipped due to final state check)\n   - If connection closes: The NetworkClient will clean up in-flight requests\n\n4. **Matches design intent**: Buffer pools are meant to manage buffer lifecycle. The accumulator should only deallocate when the batch lifecycle is truly complete (response received or connection error), not at expiration time.\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Execution Path to Race Condition\n\n1. Producer calls `Sender.run()` which calls `runOnce()`\n2. `runOnce()` calls `sendProducerData()` at line 339\n3. Batches are drained and sent via `sendProduceRequest()` (lines 395, 442)\n4. In NetworkClient, request is built and Send object is created (line 608)\n5. Send object is queued to selector, awaiting network I/O (line 617)\n6. Meanwhile, in the next `sendProducerData()` call, batch expiration is checked (line 406)\n7. Expired batch is found and removed from inFlightBatches (line 191)\n8. `failBatch()` is called, which deallocates the buffer (line 835)\n9. Buffer is returned to pool and added to free list (line 265)\n10. New batch allocates same buffer, writes to it\n11. Original Send object writes corrupted data to socket\n12. Messages intended for topic A have topic B data, or vice versa\n\n### Why CRC Passes\n\nThe CRC checksum in Kafka only covers the record key/value/headers, not the topic/partition metadata. The partition information is in the ProduceRequest header (serialized separately). When the buffer is reused mid-write, the corruption affects the message payload, but since the CRC was already embedded when the batch was created, it doesn't detect the corruption if only the buffer contents were overwritten after CRC calculation.\n\n### Impact\n\nThis bug manifests as messages silently appearing on wrong topics, especially during:\n- Network disruptions or broker restarts (causing timeouts)\n- High latency scenarios with lingering enabled (`linger.ms > 0`)\n- Burst traffic that triggers batch expiration\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":79,"oldLines":39,"newStart":79,"newLines":53,"lines":[" "," ### Implementation"," ","-The core issue is at **line 835 in Sender.java**, within the `failBatch()` method:","+The fix requires TWO changes to Sender.java to prevent deallocating buffers while they're still in-flight:"," ","+**Change 1: failBatch() - Don't deallocate immediately (line 817-836)**","+","+The core issue is at **line 835 in Sender.java**:","+"," ```java","-maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);  // UNSAFE for in-flight batches","+maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);  // UNSAFE - buffer still in-flight!"," ```"," ","-This unconditionally deallocates the buffer, but the batch's request might still be queued in the NetworkClient's `inFlightRequests` (line 616 in NetworkClient.doSend()).","+This should be changed to:"," ","-**Solution: Don't deallocate buffers in failBatch() - let completeBatch() handle it**","-","-The fix requires modifying `failBatch()` to avoid deallocating buffers for batches that are still in-flight. Drains ready batches from accumulator at line 395\n   - Adds them to inFlightBatches at line 396\n   - Calls sendProduceRequests() at line 442 to queue network sends\n\n2. **Request serialization**: `NetworkClient.doSend()` (line 551)\n   - Builds the request at line 582: `builder.build(version)`\n   - Creates Send object at line 608: `request.toSend(header)`\n   - Adds Send to inFlightRequests at line 616\n   - Queues to selector at line 617: `selector.send(new NetworkSend(...))`\n\n3. **Batch expiration check**: `Sender.sendProducerData()` (line 406-407)\n   - Calls `getExpiredInflightBatches(now)` which iterates inFlightBatches\n   - Removes expired batches from inFlightBatches at line 191\n\n4. **Batch failure handling**: `Sender.failBatch()` (line 817)\n   - Calls `batch.completeExceptionally()` at line 825\n   - Calls `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` at line 835\n\n5. **Buffer deallocation**: `RecordAccumulator.deallocate()` (line 1027)\n   - Calls `free.deallocate(batch.buffer(), batch.initialCapacity())` at line 1032\n\n6. **Buffer reuse**: `BufferPool.deallocate()` (line 260)\n   - Clears buffer at line 264: `buffer.clear()`\n   - Adds to free list at line 265: `this.free.add(buffer)`\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**File**: `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java`\n**Function**: `failBatch()` (line 817) and `sendProducerData()` (line 357)\n**Line**: ~835 (in failBatch) and ~418 (calling failBatch)\n\n### Why the Bug Occurs\n\nThe race condition happens because:\n\n1. **Request sent asynchronously**: When `sendProduceRequest()` calls `client.send()` at line 914, the request is NOT immediately written to the socket. Instead, it's queued in the NetworkClient and will be serialized and sent by the network I/O thread when the socket is ready.\n\n2. **Request holds buffer reference**: The NetworkClient's `doSend()` method (line 608) calls `request.toSend(header)` which creates a `Send` object containing references to the batch's ByteBuffer. This Send object is held in `inFlightRequests` (line 616).\n\n3. **Expired batch deallocates buffer immediately**: When `Sender.sendProducerData()` checks for expired in-flight batches (line 406-407):\n   - `getExpiredInflightBatches()` removes the batch from `inFlightBatches` (line 191)\n   - `failBatch()` is called at line 418\n   - Inside `failBatch()`, `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` is called at line 835\n   - This calls `accumulator.deallocate()` which returns the buffer to the BufferPool (line 1032)\n   - The buffer is cleared and added to the free list (line 265)\n\n4. **Buffer reused while still in-flight**: The buffer is now available in the free list, even though the Send object in NetworkClient's `inFlightRequests` still holds a reference to it and may still be writing it to the socket.\n\n5. **Corruption occurs**: A new batch allocates the same buffer from the free list (via `accumulator.allocate()`), writes its data to it, and modifies its contents. Meanwhile, the original Send object is still writing to the socket, but the buffer now contains corrupted data from the new batch.\n\n### The Core Issue\n\nThe key vulnerability is at **line 835 in Sender.java**:\n```java\nmaybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);  // Called in failBatch()\n```\n\nThis line deallocates the buffer for a batch that is still in-flight in the NetworkClient. The batch's request may still be queued in the selector, waiting to be written to the socket, or currently being written. The Send object holds a reference to the ByteBuffer, not a copy of it.\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\nThe fix requires separating buffer deallocation from batch failure handling. When a batch expires while in-flight, we should NOT deallocate its buffer immediately. Instead, we should:\n\n1. Mark the batch as failed\n2. Let the buffer remain allocated and referenced by the in-flight Send object\n3. Deallocate the buffer only when the response is received (in `completeBatch()`) or when the network connection is definitively closed\n\n### Implementation\n\nThe fix requires TWO changes to Sender.java to prevent deallocating buffers while they're still in-flight:\n\n**Change 1: failBatch() - Don't deallocate immediately (line 817-836)**\n\nThe core issue is at **line 835 in Sender.java**:\n\n```java\nmaybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);  // UNSAFE - buffer still in-flight!\n```\n\nThis should be changed to:\n\n```diff\n- maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n+ // Don't deallocate buffer here - the request is still queued in NetworkClient.\n+ // The buffer reference is held by the Send object in inFlightRequests.\n+ // We'll deallocate when the response arrives (in completeBatch) or connection closes.\n+ maybeRemoveFromInflightBatches(batch);\n```\n\n**Change 2: completeBatch() - Deallocate even if batch already failed (line 744-752)**\n\nThe response handler must deallocate buffers for batches that were already marked failed:\n\n```diff\nprivate void completeBatch(ProducerBatch batch, ProduceResponse.PartitionResponse response) {\n    if (transactionManager != null) {\n        transactionManager.handleCompletedBatch(batch, response);\n    }\n\n    if (batch.complete(response.baseOffset, response.logAppendTime)) {\n        maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n-   }\n+   } else if (batch.isDone()) {\n+       // Batch already completed (failed by failBatch due to expiration)\n+       // Still need to deallocate the buffer now that request is no longer in-flight\n+       maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n+   }\n}\n```\n\nTogether, these changes ensure:\n1. **Expired batches are marked failed immediately** (user gets error notification via `completeExceptionally()`)\n2. **Buffers remain valid until network write completes** (Send object can safely serialize the batch)\n3. **Safe deallocation happens after request is done** (when response arrives or connection closes)\n4. **No corruption occurs** because the batch's buffer is never reused while in-flight\n\n### Why This Fix is Safe\n\nThe fix is safe because:\n\n1. **No double deallocation**: When a response arrives in `completeBatch()`, it calls `batch.complete()` which checks the batch's final state (line 218). If the batch was already marked as failed by `failBatch()`, then `complete()` returns false and `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` is NOT called (line 750).\n\n2. **Prevents corruption**: By not deallocating in `failBatch()`, the buffer remains valid while the `Send` object (still in NetworkClient's `inFlightRequests`) is writing to the socket.\n\n3. **Eventual cleanup**: When the response finally arrives or the connection closes:\n   - If response arrives: `completeBatch()` handles deallocation (though skipped due to final state check)\n   - If connection closes: The NetworkClient will clean up in-flight requests\n\n4. **Matches design intent**: Buffer pools are meant to manage buffer lifecycle. The accumulator should only deallocate when the batch lifecycle is truly complete (response received or connection error), not at expiration time.\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Execution Path to Race Condition\n\n1. Producer calls `Sender.run()` which calls `runOnce()`\n2. `runOnce()` calls `sendProducerData()` at line 339\n3. Batches are drained and sent via `sendProduceRequest()` (lines 395, 442)\n4. In NetworkClient, request is built and Send object is created (line 608)\n5. Send object is queued to selector, awaiting network I/O (line 617)\n6. Meanwhile, in the next `sendProducerData()` call, batch expiration is checked (line 406)\n7. Expired batch is found and removed from inFlightBatches (line 191)\n8. `failBatch()` is called, which deallocates the buffer (line 835)\n9. Buffer is returned to pool and added to free list (line 265)\n10. New batch allocates same buffer, writes to it\n11. Original Send object writes corrupted data to socket\n12. Messages intended for topic A have topic B data, or vice versa\n\n### Why CRC Passes\n\nThe CRC checksum in Kafka only covers the record key/value/headers, not the topic/partition metadata. The partition information is in the ProduceRequest header (serialized separately). When the buffer is reused mid-write, the corruption affects the message payload, but since the CRC was already embedded when the batch was created, it doesn't detect the corruption if only the buffer contents were overwritten after CRC calculation.\n\n### Impact\n\nThis bug manifests as messages silently appearing on wrong topics, especially during:\n- Network disruptions or broker restarts (causing timeouts)\n- High latency scenarios with lingering enabled (`linger.ms > 0`)\n- Burst traffic that triggers batch expiration\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":130,"oldLines":16,"newStart":130,"newLines":24,"lines":[" "," The fix is safe because:"," ","-1. **No double deallocation**: When a response arrives in `completeBatch()`, it calls `batch.complete()` which checks the batch's final state (line 218). Drains ready batches from accumulator at line 395\n    14→   - Adds them to inFlightBatches at line 396\n    15→   - Calls sendProduceRequests() at line 442 to queue network sends\n    16→\n    17→2. **Request serialization**: `NetworkClient.doSend()` (line 551)\n    18→   - Builds the request at line 582: `builder.build(version)`\n    19→   - Creates Send object at line 608: `request.toSend(header)`\n    20→   - Adds Send to inFlightRequests at line 616\n    21→   - Queues to selector at line 617: `selector.send(new NetworkSend(...))`\n    22→\n    23→3. **Batch expiration check**: `Sender.sendProducerData()` (line 406-407)\n    24→   - Calls `getExpiredInflightBatches(now)` which iterates inFlightBatches\n    25→   - Removes expired batches from inFlightBatches at line 191\n    26→\n    27→4. **Batch failure handling**: `Sender.failBatch()` (line 817)\n    28→   - Adds to free list at line 265: `this.free.add(buffer)`\n    37→\n    38→## Root Cause\n    39→\n    40→**File**: `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java`\n    41→**Function**: `failBatch()` (line 817) and `sendProducerData()` (line 357)\n    42→**Line**: ~835 (in failBatch) and ~418 (calling failBatch)\n    43→\n    44→### Why the Bug Occurs\n    45→\n    46→The race condition happens because:\n    47→\n    48→1. **Request sent asynchronously**: When `sendProduceRequest()` calls `client.send()` at line 914, the request is NOT immediately written to the socket. Instead, it's queued in the NetworkClient and will be serialized and sent by the network I/O thread when the socket is ready.\n    49→\n    50→2. **Request holds buffer reference**: The NetworkClient's `doSend()` method (line 608) calls `request.toSend(header)` which creates a `Send` object containing references to the batch's ByteBuffer. This Send object is held in `inFlightRequests` (line 616).\n    51→\n    52→3. **Expired batch deallocates buffer immediately**: When `Sender.sendProducerData()` checks for expired in-flight batches (line 406-407):\n    53→   - `getExpiredInflightBatches()` removes the batch from `inFlightBatches` (line 191)\n    54→   - `failBatch()` is called at line 418\n    55→   - Inside `failBatch()`, `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` is called at line 835\n    56→   - This calls `accumulator.deallocate()` which returns the buffer to the BufferPool (line 1032)\n    57→   - The buffer is cleared and added to the free list (line 265)\n    58→\n    59→4. **Buffer reused while still in-flight**: The buffer is now available in the free list, even though the Send object in NetworkClient's `inFlightRequests` still holds a reference to it and may still be writing it to the socket.\n    60→\n    61→5. **Corruption occurs**: A new batch allocates the same buffer from the free list (via `accumulator.allocate()`), writes its data to it, and modifies its contents. Meanwhile, the original Send object is still writing to the socket, but the buffer now contains corrupted data from the new batch.\n    62→\n    63→### The Core Issue\n    64→\n    65→The key vulnerability is at **line 835 in Sender.java**:\n    66→```java\n    67→maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);  // Called in failBatch()\n    68→```\n    69→\n    70→This line deallocates the buffer for a batch that is still in-flight in the NetworkClient. The batch's request may still be queued in the selector, waiting to be written to the socket, or currently being written. The Send object holds a reference to the ByteBuffer, not a copy of it.\n    71→\n    72→## Proposed Fix\n    73→\n    74→The fix requires separating buffer deallocation from batch failure handling. When a batch expires while in-flight, we should NOT deallocate its buffer immediately. Instead, we should:\n    75→\n    76→1. Mark the batch as failed\n    77→2. Let the buffer remain allocated and referenced by the in-flight Send object\n    78→3. Deallocate the buffer only when the response is received (in `completeBatch()`) or when the network connection is definitively closed\n    79→\n    80→### Implementation\n    81→\n    82→The fix requires TWO changes to Sender.java to prevent deallocating buffers while they're still in-flight:\n    83→\n    84→**Change 1: failBatch() - Don't deallocate immediately (line 817-836)**\n    85→\n    86→The core issue is at **line 835 in Sender.java**:\n    87→\n    88→```java\n    89→maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);  // UNSAFE - buffer still in-flight!\n    90→```\n    91→\n    92→This should be changed to:\n    93→\n    94→```diff\n    95→- maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n    96→+ // Don't deallocate buffer here - the request is still queued in NetworkClient.\n    97→+ // The buffer reference is held by the Send object in inFlightRequests.\n    98→+ // We'll deallocate when the response arrives (in completeBatch) or connection closes.\n    99→+ maybeRemoveFromInflightBatches(batch);\n   100→```\n   101→\n   102→**Change 2: completeBatch() - Deallocate even if batch already failed (line 744-752)**\n   103→\n   104→The response handler must deallocate buffers for batches that were already marked failed:\n   105→\n   106→```diff\n   107→private void completeBatch(ProducerBatch batch, ProduceResponse.PartitionResponse response) {\n   108→    if (transactionManager != null) {\n   109→        transactionManager.handleCompletedBatch(batch, response);\n   110→    }\n   111→\n   112→    if (batch.complete(response.baseOffset, response.logAppendTime)) {\n   113→        maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n   114→-   }\n   115→+   } else if (batch.isDone()) {\n   116→+       // Batch already completed (failed by failBatch due to expiration)\n   117→+       // Still need to deallocate the buffer now that request is no longer in-flight\n   118→+       maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n   119→+   }\n   120→}\n   121→```\n   122→\n   123→Together, these changes ensure:\n   124→1. **Expired batches are marked failed immediately** (user gets error notification via `completeExceptionally()`)\n   125→2. **Buffers remain valid until network write completes** (Send object can safely serialize the batch)\n   126→3. **Safe deallocation happens after request is done** (when response arrives or connection closes)\n   127→4. **No corruption occurs** because the batch's buffer is never reused while in-flight\n   128→\n   129→### Why This Fix is Safe\n   130→\n   131→The fix is safe because:\n   132→\n   133→1. **Prevents corruption**: By not deallocating in `failBatch()`, the buffer remains valid while the `Send` object (in NetworkClient's `inFlightRequests` at line 616) is writing to the socket. New batches cannot reuse the buffer until the network layer releases it.\n   134→\n   135→2. **No double deallocation**: The new `else if` condition in `completeBatch()` ensures we only deallocate once:\n   136→   - Successful response: `batch.complete()` returns true and deallocates\n   137→   - Failed response after batch still in-flight: `batch.complete()` returns false, but `batch.isDone()` is true, so we deallocate\n   138→   - No path deallocates twice\n   139→\n   140→3. **Immediate error notification**: Users still get immediate timeout exceptions via `batch.completeExceptionally()` in `failBatch()`, so the error is reported right away even though deallocation is delayed.\n   141→\n   142→4. **Eventual cleanup guaranteed**:\n   143→   - Normal case: Response arrives → `completeBatch()` deallocates\n   144→   - Network error: Connection closes → NetworkClient discards Send object → buffer eventually cleaned up\n   145→   - Connection timeout: Request times out → NetworkClient removes from `inFlightRequests` → can be deallocated\n   146→\n   147→5. **Handles all failBatch() call sites**:\n   148→   - Expired batches (line 418): Buffer stays alive until response or timeout\n   149→   - Error responses (line 720): Buffer already no longer in-flight, `completeBatch()` handles it\n   150→\n   151→## Analysis\n   152→\n   153→### Execution Path to Race Condition\n   154→\n   155→1. Producer calls `Sender.run()` which calls `runOnce()`\n   156→2. `runOnce()` calls `sendProducerData()` at line 339\n   157→3. Batches are drained and sent via `sendProduceRequest()` (lines 395, 442)\n   158→4. In NetworkClient, request is built and Send object is created (line 608)\n   159→5. Send object is queued to selector, awaiting network I/O (line 617)\n   160→6. Meanwhile, in the next `sendProducerData()` call, batch expiration is checked (line 406)\n   161→7. Expired batch is found and removed from inFlightBatches (line 191)\n   162→8. `failBatch()` is called, which deallocates the buffer (line 835)\n   163→9. Buffer is returned to pool and added to free list (line 265)\n   164→10. New batch allocates same buffer, writes to it\n   165→11. Original Send object writes corrupted data to socket\n   166→12. Messages intended for topic A have topic B data, or vice versa\n   167→\n   168→### Why CRC Passes\n   169→\n   170→The CRC checksum in Kafka only covers the record key/value/headers, not the topic/partition metadata. The partition information is in the ProduceRequest header (serialized separately). When the buffer is reused mid-write, the corruption affects the message payload, but since the CRC was already embedded when the batch was created, it doesn't detect the corruption if only the buffer contents were overwritten after CRC calculation.\n   171→\n   172→### Impact\n   173→\n   174→This bug manifests as messages silently appearing on wrong topics, especially during:\n   175→- Network disruptions or broker restarts (causing timeouts)\n   176→- High latency scenarios with lingering enabled (`linger.ms > 0`)\n   177→- Burst traffic that triggers batch expiration\n   178→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. Let the buffer remain allocated and referenced by the in-flight Send object\n3. Deallocate the buffer only when the response is received (in `completeBatch()`) or when the network connection is definitively closed\n\n### Implementation\n\nThe fix requires TWO changes to Sender.java to prevent deallocating buffers while they're still in-flight:\n\n**Change 1: failBatch() - Don't deallocate immediately (line 817-836)**\n\nThe core issue is at **line 835 in Sender.java**:\n\n```java\nmaybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);  // UNSAFE - buffer still in-flight!\n```\n\nThis should be changed to:\n\n```diff\n- maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n+ // Don't deallocate buffer here - the request is still queued in NetworkClient.\n+ // The buffer reference is held by the Send object in inFlightRequests.\n+ // We'll deallocate when the response arrives (in completeBatch) or connection closes.\n+ maybeRemoveFromInflightBatches(batch);\n```\n\n**Change 2: completeBatch() - Deallocate even if batch already failed (line 744-752)**\n\nThe response handler must deallocate buffers for batches that were already marked failed:\n\n```diff\nprivate void completeBatch(ProducerBatch batch, ProduceResponse.PartitionResponse response) {\n    if (transactionManager != null) {\n        transactionManager.handleCompletedBatch(batch, response);\n    }\n\n    if (batch.complete(response.baseOffset, response.logAppendTime)) {\n        maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n-   }\n+   } else if (batch.isDone()) {\n+       // Batch already completed (failed by failBatch due to expiration)\n+       // Still need to deallocate the buffer now that request is no longer in-flight\n+       maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n+   }\n}\n```\n\nTogether, these changes ensure:\n1. **Expired batches are marked failed immediately** (user gets error notification via `completeExceptionally()`)\n2. **Buffers remain valid until network write completes** (Send object can safely serialize the batch)\n3. **Safe deallocation happens after request is done** (when response arrives or connection closes)\n4. **No corruption occurs** because the batch's buffer is never reused while in-flight\n\n### Why This Fix is Safe\n\nThe fix is safe because:\n\n1. **Prevents corruption**: By not deallocating in `failBatch()`, the buffer remains valid while the `Send` object (in NetworkClient's `inFlightRequests` at line 616) is writing to the socket. New batches cannot reuse the buffer until the network layer releases it.\n\n2. **No double deallocation**: The new `else if` condition in `completeBatch()` ensures we only deallocate once:\n   - Successful response: `batch.complete()` returns true and deallocates\n   - Failed response after batch still in-flight: `batch.complete()` returns false, but `batch.isDone()` is true, so we deallocate\n   - No path deallocates twice\n\n3. **Immediate error notification**: Users still get immediate timeout exceptions via `batch.completeExceptionally()` in `failBatch()`, so the error is reported right away even though deallocation is delayed.\n\n4. **Eventual cleanup guaranteed**:\n   - Normal case: Response arrives → `completeBatch()` deallocates\n   - Network error: Connection closes → NetworkClient discards Send object → buffer eventually cleaned up\n   - Connection timeout: Request times out → NetworkClient removes from `inFlightRequests` → can be deallocated\n\n5. **Handles all failBatch() call sites**:\n   - Expired batches (line 418): Buffer stays alive until response or timeout\n   - Error responses (line 720): Buffer already no longer in-flight, `completeBatch()` handles it\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Execution Path to Race Condition\n\n1. Producer calls `Sender.run()` which calls `runOnce()`\n2. `runOnce()` calls `sendProducerData()` at line 339\n3. Batches are drained and sent via `sendProduceRequest()` (lines 395, 442)\n4. In NetworkClient, request is built and Send object is created (line 608)\n5. Send object is queued to selector, awaiting network I/O (line 617)\n6. Meanwhile, in the next `sendProducerData()` call, batch expiration is checked (line 406)\n7. Expired batch is found and removed from inFlightBatches (line 191)\n8. `failBatch()` is called, which deallocates the buffer (line 835)\n9. Buffer is returned to pool and added to free list (line 265)\n10. New batch allocates same buffer, writes to it\n11. Original Send object writes corrupted data to socket\n12. Messages intended for topic A have topic B data, or vice versa\n\n### Why CRC Passes\n\nThe CRC checksum in Kafka only covers the record key/value/headers, not the topic/partition metadata. The partition information is in the ProduceRequest header (serialized separately). When the buffer is reused mid-write, the corruption affects the message payload, but since the CRC was already embedded when the batch was created, it doesn't detect the corruption if only the buffer contents were overwritten after CRC calculation.\n\n### Impact\n\nThis bug manifests as messages silently appearing on wrong topics, especially during:\n- Network disruptions or broker restarts (causing timeouts)\n- High latency scenarios with lingering enabled (`linger.ms > 0`)\n- Burst traffic that triggers batch expiration\n","numLines":178,"startLine":1,"totalLines":178}}}
